	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Helena Bonham Carter</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">British actress</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This <a href="/wiki/Double-barrelled_name#British_tradition" title="Double-barrelled name">British surname is barrelled</a>, being made up of multiple names. It should be written as <i><a href="/wiki/Bonham_Carter" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonham Carter">Bonham Carter</a></i>, not <i><a href="/wiki/Carter_(name)" title="Carter (name)">Carter</a></i>.</div>
<table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div class="fn" style="display:inline">Helena Bonham at the <a href="/wiki/83rd_Academy_Awards" title="83rd Academy Awards">83rd Academy Awards</a> in 2011</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td><span style="display:none"> (<span <p><b>Helena Bonham Carter</b> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born 26 May 1966) is an English actress. She is known for her roles in both low-budget <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">art films</a> and large-scale <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">blockbusters</a>. She was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Actress">Academy Award for Best Actress</a> for her role as Kate Croy in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wings_of_the_Dove_(1997_film)" title="The Wings of the Dove (1997 film)">The Wings of the Dove</a></i> (1997). For her role as <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">Queen Elizabeth</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Speech" title="The King&#39;s Speech">The King's Speech</a></i> (2010), she was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role</a>. She also won the 2010 <a href="/wiki/International_Emmy_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="International Emmy Award for Best Actress">International Emmy Award for Best Actress</a> for her role as British author <a href="/wiki/Enid_Blyton" title="Enid Blyton">Enid Blyton</a> in the TV film <i><a href="/wiki/Enid_(film)" title="Enid (film)">Enid</a></i> (2009).
</p><p>Bonham Carter began her film career, playing the <a href="/wiki/Lady_Jane_Grey" title="Lady Jane Grey">title character</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Jane_(1986_film)" title="Lady Jane (1986 film)">Lady Jane</a></i> (1986), and playing Lucy Honeychurch in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Room_with_a_View_(1985_film)" title="A Room with a View (1985 film)">A Room with a View</a></i> (1985). Her other film roles include <a href="/wiki/Ophelia" title="Ophelia">Ophelia</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(1990_film)" title="Hamlet (1990 film)">Hamlet</a></i> (1990), <i><a href="/wiki/Where_Angels_Fear_to_Tread_(film)" title="Where Angels Fear to Tread (film)">Where Angels Fear to Tread</a></i> (1991), <i><a href="/wiki/Howards_End_(film)" title="Howards End (film)">Howards End</a></i> (1992), <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Lavenza" title="Elizabeth Lavenza">Elizabeth Lavenza</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelley%27s_Frankenstein_(film)" title="Mary Shelley&#39;s Frankenstein (film)">Mary Shelley's Frankenstein</a></i> (1994), <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mighty_Aphrodite" title="Mighty Aphrodite">Mighty Aphrodite</a></i> (1995), Marla Singer in <i><a href="/wiki/Fight_Club" title="Fight Club">Fight Club</a></i> (1999), <a href="/wiki/Bellatrix_Lestrange" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellatrix Lestrange">Bellatrix Lestrange</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">Harry Potter</a></i> series (2007–11), <a href="/wiki/Skynet_(Terminator)" title="Skynet (Terminator)">Skynet</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator_Salvation" title="Terminator Salvation">Terminator Salvation</a></i> (2009), <a href="/wiki/Miss_Havisham" title="Miss Havisham">Miss Havisham</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Expectations_(2012_film)" title="Great Expectations (2012 film)">Great Expectations</a></i> (2012), <a href="/wiki/Mme._Th%C3%A9nardier" class="mw-redirect" title="Mme. Thénardier">Madame Thénardier</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(2012_film)" title="Les Misérables (2012 film)">Les Misérables</a></i> (2012), the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%27s_Cinderella_characters#The_Fairy_Godmother" title="List of Disney&#39;s Cinderella characters">Fairy Godmother</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(2015_Disney_film)" title="Cinderella (2015 Disney film)">Cinderella</a></i> (2015) and Rose Weil in <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_8" title="Ocean&#39;s 8">Ocean's 8</a></i> (2018). She has frequently collaborated with director <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a>; in <i><a href="/wiki/Planet_of_the_Apes_(2001_film)" title="Planet of the Apes (2001 film)">Planet of the Apes</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Fish" title="Big Fish">Big Fish</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/Corpse_Bride" title="Corpse Bride">Corpse Bride</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_(film)" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (film)">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i> (2007) where she played <a href="/wiki/Mrs._Lovett" title="Mrs. Lovett">Mrs. Lovett</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Shadows_(film)" title="Dark Shadows (film)">Dark Shadows</a></i> (2012), and playing the <a href="/wiki/Red_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="Red Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">Red Queen</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> (2010) and its sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_Through_the_Looking_Glass_(2016_film)" title="Alice Through the Looking Glass (2016 film)">Alice Through the Looking Glass</a></i> (2016). Her other <a href="/wiki/Television_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Television films">television films</a> include <i><a href="/wiki/A_Pattern_of_Roses" title="A Pattern of Roses">A Pattern of Roses</a></i> (1983), <i><a href="/wiki/Fatal_Deception:_Mrs._Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Fatal Deception: Mrs. Lee Harvey Oswald">Fatal Deception: Mrs. Lee Harvey Oswald</a></i> (1993), <i><a href="/wiki/Live_from_Baghdad_(film)" title="Live from Baghdad (film)">Live from Baghdad</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Toast_(film)" title="Toast (film)">Toast</a></i> (2010), and <i><a href="/wiki/Burton_%26_Taylor" title="Burton &amp; Taylor">Burton &amp; Taylor</a></i> (2013). In 2018, she was confirmed to play <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret,_Countess_of_Snowdon" title="Princess Margaret, Countess of Snowdon">Princess Margaret</a> on seasons three and four of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Crown (TV series)">The Crown</a></i>.
</p><p>She was made a <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in the <a href="/wiki/2012_New_Year_Honours" title="2012 New Year Honours">2012 New Year Honours</a> list for services to drama,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and in January 2014, the British prime minister, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, announced that Bonham Carter had been appointed to Britain's new national <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-Dysch_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dysch-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bonham Carter was born in <a href="/wiki/Islington" title="Islington">Islington</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Her father, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Bonham_Carter" title="Raymond Bonham Carter">Raymond Bonham Carter</a>, who came from a prominent <a href="/wiki/Bonham_Carter_family" title="Bonham Carter family">British political family</a>, was a <a href="/wiki/Merchant_bank" title="Merchant bank">merchant banker</a> and served as the alternative British director representing the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in Washington, D.C., during the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Costa2006-11-03_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costa2006-11-03-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FilmReference_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmReference-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Her mother, Elena (née Propper de Callejón), is a psychotherapist who is of three quarters <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> background, and whose own parents were diplomat <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Propper_de_Callej%C3%B3n" title="Eduardo Propper de Callejón">Eduardo Propper de Callejón</a> and painter <a href="/wiki/Fould_family" title="Fould family">Baroness Hélène Fould-Springer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Costa2006-11-03_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costa2006-11-03-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JJ_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JJ-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter's paternal grandmother was politician and feminist <a href="/wiki/Violet_Bonham_Carter" title="Violet Bonham Carter">Violet Bonham Carter</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> during the first half of the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonham Carter is the youngest of three children, with two brothers, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Bonham_Carter" title="Edward Bonham Carter">Edward</a> and Thomas. They were brought up in <a href="/wiki/Golders_Green" title="Golders Green">Golders Green</a> and she was educated at <a href="/wiki/South_Hampstead_High_School" title="South Hampstead High School">South Hampstead High School</a>, and completed her <a href="/wiki/A-level" class="mw-redirect" title="A-level">A-levels</a> at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_School" title="Westminster School">Westminster School</a>. Bonham Carter was denied admission to <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="King&#39;s College, Cambridge">King's College, Cambridge</a>, not because of her academic performance but because college officials were afraid that she would leave during the course to pursue her acting career.<sup id="cite_ref-scotsman1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotsman1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Bonham Carter was five, her mother had a serious nervous breakdown, which took three years for recovery. Soon afterwards, her mother's experience in therapy led her to become a psychotherapist herself—Bonham Carter has since paid her to read her scripts and deliver opinions on the characters' psychological motivations.<sup id="cite_ref-globemail1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globemail1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Five years after her mother's recovery, her father was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_neuroma" class="mw-redirect" title="Acoustic neuroma">acoustic neuroma</a>. He suffered complications during an operation to remove the tumour that led to a stroke that left him half-paralysed and using a wheelchair.<sup id="cite_ref-times1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> With her brothers at college, Bonham Carter was left to help her mother cope. She later studied her father's movements and mannerisms for her role in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Theory_of_Flight" title="The Theory of Flight">The Theory of Flight</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He died in January 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bonham Carter, who has no formal acting training,<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> entered the field winning a national writing contest (1979) and used the money to pay for her entry into the actors' <i>Spotlight</i> directory. She made her professional acting début at the age of 16 in a television commercial. She also had a part in a minor TV film, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Pattern_of_Roses" title="A Pattern of Roses">A Pattern of Roses</a></i>.
</p><p>Her first lead film role was as <a href="/wiki/Lady_Jane_Grey" title="Lady Jane Grey">Lady Jane Grey</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Lady_Jane_(1986_film)" title="Lady Jane (1986 film)">Lady Jane</a></i> (1986), which was given mixed reviews by critics. Her <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_role" title="Breakthrough role">breakthrough role</a> was Lucy Honeychurch in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Room_with_a_View_(1985_film)" title="A Room with a View (1985 film)">A Room with a View</a></i> (1985), which was filmed after <i>Lady Jane</i> but released two months earlier. Bonham Carter also appeared in episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_Vice" title="Miami Vice">Miami Vice</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Don_Johnson" title="Don Johnson">Don Johnson</a>'s love interest during the 1986–87 season and then, in 1987 with <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Bogarde" title="Dirk Bogarde">Dirk Bogarde</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Vision_(TV_Movie)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Vision (TV Movie)">The Vision</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Granger" title="Stewart Granger">Stewart Granger</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hazard_of_Hearts" title="A Hazard of Hearts">A Hazard of Hearts</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/John_Gielgud" title="John Gielgud">John Gielgud</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Getting_It_Right_(film)" title="Getting It Right (film)">Getting It Right</a></i>. Bonham Carter was originally cast in the role of Bess McNeill in <i><a href="/wiki/Breaking_the_Waves" title="Breaking the Waves">Breaking the Waves</a></i>, but backed out during production due to "the character's painful psychic and physical exposure", according to <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ebert1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ebert1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The role went to <a href="/wiki/Emily_Watson" title="Emily Watson">Emily Watson</a>, who was nominated for an Academy Award for her performance.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, Bonham Carter appeared in a dream sequence during the second series of the British sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Absolutely_Fabulous" title="Absolutely Fabulous">Absolutely Fabulous</a></i>, as <a href="/wiki/Edina_Monsoon" title="Edina Monsoon">Edina Monsoon</a>'s daughter Saffron, who was normally played by <a href="/wiki/Julia_Sawalha" title="Julia Sawalha">Julia Sawalha</a>. Throughout the series, references were made to Saffron's resemblance to Bonham Carter.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her early films led to her being typecast as a "<a href="/wiki/Corset" title="Corset">corset</a> queen", and "<a href="/wiki/English_rose_(epithet)" title="English rose (epithet)">English rose</a>", playing pre- and early 20th century characters, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Merchant-Ivory" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant-Ivory">Merchant-Ivory</a> films. She played Olivia in <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Nunn" title="Trevor Nunn">Trevor Nunn</a>'s film version of <i><a href="/wiki/Twelfth_Night" title="Twelfth Night">Twelfth Night</a></i> in 1996. One of the high points of her early career was her performance as the scheming Kate Croy in the 1997 film adaption of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wings_of_the_Dove_(1997_film)" title="The Wings of the Dove (1997 film)">The Wings of the Dove</a></i> which was highly acclaimed internationally and netted her first Golden Globe and Academy Award nominations. She has since expanded her range,<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> with her more recent films being <i><a href="/wiki/Fight_Club" title="Fight Club">Fight Club</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wallace_%26_Gromit:_The_Curse_of_the_Were-Rabbit" title="Wallace &amp; Gromit: The Curse of the Were-Rabbit">Wallace &amp; Gromit: The Curse of the Were-Rabbit</a></i>, and her then-partner <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_(film)" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (film)">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Corpse_Bride" title="Corpse Bride">Corpse Bride</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Fish" title="Big Fish">Big Fish</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_career">Later career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Later career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg/170px-Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg/255px-Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Helena_Bonham_Carter_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonham Carter at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a>, promoting <i><a href="/wiki/Wallace_%26_Gromit:_The_Curse_of_the_Were-Rabbit" title="Wallace &amp; Gromit: The Curse of the Were-Rabbit">Wallace &amp; Gromit: The Curse of the Were-Rabbit</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Bonham Carter speaks French fluently, and starred in a 1996 French film <i>Portraits chinois</i>. In August 2001, she was featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Maxim_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Maxim magazine">Maxim</a>.</i> She played her second Queen of England when she was cast as <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a> in the ITV1 mini-series <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_(TV_serial)" title="Henry VIII (TV serial)">Henry&#160;VIII</a></i>; however, her role was restricted, as she was pregnant with her first child at the time of filming.<sup id="cite_ref-express1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-express1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter was a member of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2006 Cannes Film Festival">2006 Cannes Film Festival</a> jury that unanimously selected <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wind_That_Shakes_the_Barley_(film)" title="The Wind That Shakes the Barley (film)">The Wind That Shakes the Barley</a></i> as best film.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2006, Bonham Carter launched her own fashion line, "The Pantaloonies", with swimwear designer Samantha Sage. Their first collection, called Bloomin' Bloomers, is a <a href="/wiki/Victorian_fashion" title="Victorian fashion">Victorian</a> style selection of <a href="/wiki/Camisoles" class="mw-redirect" title="Camisoles">camisoles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mob_cap" title="Mob cap">mob caps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bloomers_(clothing)" title="Bloomers (clothing)">bloomers</a>. The duo worked on Pantaloonies customised jeans, which Bonham Carter describes as "a kind of scrapbook on the bum".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonham Carter played <a href="/wiki/Bellatrix_Lestrange" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellatrix Lestrange">Bellatrix Lestrange</a> in the final four <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</a> (2007–2011). While filming <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, she accidentally ruptured the eardrum of <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Lewis_(actor)" title="Matthew Lewis (actor)">Matthew Lewis</a> (playing <a href="/wiki/Neville_Longbottom" class="mw-redirect" title="Neville Longbottom">Neville Longbottom</a>) when she stuck her wand in his ear.<sup id="cite_ref-daly_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daly-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter received positive reviews as Bellatrix, described as a "shining but underused talent".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-daly_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daly-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> She played <a href="/wiki/Mrs._Lovett" title="Mrs. Lovett">Mrs. Lovett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd" title="Sweeney Todd">Sweeney Todd</a>'s (<a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>) amorous accomplice in the film adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim" title="Stephen Sondheim">Stephen Sondheim</a>'s Broadway musical, <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i>, directed by Tim Burton.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter received a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_-_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress - Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe for Best Actress</a> for her performance. She won the Best Actress award in the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Evening_Standard_British_Film_Awards" title="Evening Standard British Film Awards">Evening Standard British Film Awards</a> for her performances in <i>Sweeney Todd</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Conversations_With_Other_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Conversations With Other Women">Conversations With Other Women</a></i>, along with another Best Actress award at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Empire_Awards_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire Awards 2009">Empire Awards</a>. Bonham Carter also appeared in the fourth <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator_(franchise)" title="Terminator (franchise)">Terminator</a></i> film entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator_Salvation" title="Terminator Salvation">Terminator Salvation</a></i>, playing a small but pivotal role.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonham Carter joined the cast of Tim Burton's 2010 film, <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> as <a href="/wiki/Red_Queen_(Through_the_Looking_Glass)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Queen (Through the Looking Glass)">The Red Queen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She appears alongside <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mia_Wasikowska" title="Mia Wasikowska">Mia Wasikowska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crispin_Glover" title="Crispin Glover">Crispin Glover</a> and Harry Potter co-star <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a>. Her role was an amalgamation of <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Hearts_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Queen of Hearts (Alice&#39;s Adventures in Wonderland)">The Queen of Hearts</a> and The Red Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In early 2009, Bonham Carter was named one of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a>'</i>s top 10 British Actresses of all time. She appeared on the list with fellow actresses <a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mirren" title="Helen Mirren">Helen Mirren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Smith" title="Maggie Smith">Maggie Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Audrey_Hepburn" title="Audrey Hepburn">Audrey Hepburn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man and woman standing side by side" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3079" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Firth_and_Helena_Bonham_Carter_filming_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonham Carter and <a href="/wiki/Colin_Firth" title="Colin Firth">Colin Firth</a> in the 2010 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Speech" title="The King&#39;s Speech">The King's Speech</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In 2010, Bonham Carter played <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">Lady Elizabeth Bowes-Lyon/Queen Elizabeth</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Speech" title="The King&#39;s Speech">The King's Speech</a>.</i> As of January&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, she had received numerous plaudits and praise for her performance, including nominations for the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role">BAFTA Award for Best Actress in a Supporting Role</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KingsSpeech_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KingsSpeech-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> She won her first BAFTA Award, but lost the Academy Award to <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Leo" title="Melissa Leo">Melissa Leo</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fighter" title="The Fighter">The Fighter</a></i>.
</p><p>Bonham Carter signed to play author <a href="/wiki/Enid_Blyton" title="Enid Blyton">Enid Blyton</a> in the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">BBC Four</a> television <a href="/wiki/Biographical_film" title="Biographical film">biopic</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Enid_(film)" title="Enid (film)">Enid</a></i>. It was the first depiction of Blyton's life on the screen, and Bonham Carter starred with <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Macfadyen" title="Matthew Macfadyen">Matthew Macfadyen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denis_Lawson" title="Denis Lawson">Denis Lawson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> She received her first Television <a href="/wiki/BAFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a> Nomination for Best Actress, for <i>Enid</i>. In 2010, she starred with <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Highmore" title="Freddie Highmore">Freddie Highmore</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Slater" title="Nigel Slater">Nigel Slater</a> biopic <i><a href="/wiki/Toast_(film)" title="Toast (film)">Toast</a></i>, which was filmed in the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(county)" title="West Midlands (county)">West Midlands</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and received a gala at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="Berlin International Film Festival">Berlin International Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> She received the Britannia Award for British Artist of the Year from <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Awards" title="Britannia Awards">BAFTA LA</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Bonham Carter appeared as <a href="/wiki/Miss_Havisham" title="Miss Havisham">Miss Havisham</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>'s adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Expectations_(2012_film)" title="Great Expectations (2012 film)">Great Expectations</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In April 2012, she appeared in <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Wainwright" title="Rufus Wainwright">Rufus Wainwright</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for his single "Out of the Game", featured on the album of <a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Game" title="Out of the Game">the same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter co-starred in a <a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(2012_film)" title="Les Misérables (2012 film)">film adaptation</a> of the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables_(musical)" title="Les Misérables (musical)">Les Misérables</a></i>, released in 2012. She played the role of <a href="/wiki/Madame_Th%C3%A9nardier" class="mw-redirect" title="Madame Thénardier">Madame Thénardier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 May 2012, it was announced that Bonham Carter would be appearing in the 2013 adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Reif_Larsen" title="Reif Larsen">Reif Larsen</a>'s book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Selected_Works_of_T.S._Spivet" class="mw-redirect" title="The Selected Works of T.S. Spivet">The Selected Works of T.S. Spivet</a></i>, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_and_Prodigious_T.S._Spivet" title="The Young and Prodigious T.S. Spivet">The Young and Prodigious T.S. Spivet</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Her casting was announced alongside that of <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Bates" title="Kathy Bates">Kathy Bates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Catlett" title="Kyle Catlett">Kyle Catlett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Callum_Keith_Rennie" title="Callum Keith Rennie">Callum Keith Rennie</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Jeunet" title="Jean-Pierre Jeunet">Jean-Pierre Jeunet</a> directing.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> She also appeared in a short film directed by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polanski</a> for the clothing brand <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a>. The short was entitled <i><a href="/wiki/A_Therapy" title="A Therapy">A Therapy</a></i> and she appeared as a therapy patient to <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a>'s therapist.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, she played Red Harrington, a peg-legged brothel madam, who assists Reid and Tonto in locating Cavendish, in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lone_Ranger_(2013_film)" title="The Lone Ranger (2013 film)">The Lone Ranger</a></i>. Also that year, Bonham Carter narrated poetry for <i>The Love Book App</i>, an interactive <a href="/wiki/Anthology" title="Anthology">anthology</a> of love literature developed by <a href="/wiki/Allie_Byrne_Esiri" class="mw-redirect" title="Allie Byrne Esiri">Allie Byrne Esiri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2013, Bonham Carter appeared as <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Taylor" title="Elizabeth Taylor">Elizabeth Taylor</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Dominic_West" title="Dominic West">Dominic West</a> as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Burton" title="Richard Burton">Richard Burton</a>, in BBC4's <i><a href="/wiki/Burton_%26_Taylor" title="Burton &amp; Taylor">Burton &amp; Taylor</a></i> which premiered at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hamptons_International_Film_Festival" title="Hamptons International Film Festival">Hamptons International Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> She played the Fairy Godmother in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(2015_Disney_film)" title="Cinderella (2015 Disney film)">live-action re-imagining</a> of <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Bonham Carter reprised her role of the Red Queen in <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_Through_the_Looking_Glass_(2016_film)" title="Alice Through the Looking Glass (2016 film)">Alice Through the Looking Glass</a></i>. In June 2018, Bonham Carter starred in a spin-off of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Trilogy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ocean&#39;s Trilogy">Ocean's Eleven Trilogy</a></i>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_8" title="Ocean&#39;s 8">Ocean's 8</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Bullock" title="Sandra Bullock">Sandra Bullock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Paulson" title="Sarah Paulson">Sarah Paulson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> She is set to play an older <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret,_Countess_of_Snowdon" title="Princess Margaret, Countess of Snowdon">Princess Margaret</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_(TV_series)" title="The Crown (TV series)">The Crown</a></i>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Kirby" title="Vanessa Kirby">Vanessa Kirby</a> who played a younger version for the first two seasons.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg/170px-Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg/255px-Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg/340px-Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="467" data-file-height="829" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Helena_Bonham_Carter_SBIFF_Rush_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonham Carter at the 26th <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_International_Film_Festival" title="Santa Barbara International Film Festival">Santa Barbara International Film Festival</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes_and_politics">Causes and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Causes and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early October 2008, it was reported that Bonham Carter had become a <a href="/wiki/Patron" class="mw-redirect" title="Patron">patron</a> of the charity Action Duchenne, the national charity established to support parents and sufferers of <a href="/wiki/Duchenne_muscular_dystrophy" title="Duchenne muscular dystrophy">Duchenne muscular dystrophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2014, Bonham Carter was one of 200 public figures who were signatories to a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> opposing <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a> in the run-up to September's <a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">referendum on that issue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Bonham Carter said she was keen on the UK remaining in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in regards to the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">referendum</a> on that issue.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_tragedy">Family tragedy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Family tragedy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 2008, four of her relatives were killed in a <a href="/wiki/Safari" title="Safari">safari</a> bus crash in South Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-relative_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relative-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and she was given indefinite leave from filming <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator_Salvation" title="Terminator Salvation">Terminator Salvation</a></i>, returning later to complete filming.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenneth_Branagh">Kenneth Branagh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kenneth Branagh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1994, Bonham Carter and <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Branagh" title="Kenneth Branagh">Kenneth Branagh</a> met while filming <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Shelley%27s_Frankenstein_(film)" title="Mary Shelley&#39;s Frankenstein (film)">Mary Shelley's Frankenstein</a></i>. They began an affair, while Branagh was still married to <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thompson" title="Emma Thompson">Emma Thompson</a>, whom he had met in 1987 while filming the BBC Series <i><a href="/wiki/Fortunes_of_War_(TV_series)" title="Fortunes of War (TV series)">Fortunes of War</a></i> and married in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> At the time, Thompson's career was soaring, while Branagh was struggling to make a success of his first big-budget film (<i>Mary Shelley's Frankenstein</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Following his affair with Bonham Carter, Branagh and Thompson divorced in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> However, in 1999, after five years together, Bonham Carter and Branagh also separated.<sup id="cite_ref-forgave_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forgave-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thompson has gone on to have "no hard feelings" towards Bonham Carter, calling the past "blood under the bridge."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> She explained, "You can't hold on to anything like that. It's pointless. I haven't got the energy for it. Helena and I made our peace years and years ago. She's a wonderful woman."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Thompson, Branagh, and Bonham Carter all later went on to star together in the <i>Harry Potter</i> series, albeit in different films.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tim_Burton">Tim Burton</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tim Burton">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_(30402126)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_%2830402126%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_Premier_(30402126)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonham Carter at the premiere of Tim Burton's <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_(film)" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (film)">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a></i> in 2005</div></div></div>
<p>In 2001, Bonham Carter began a relationship with American director <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a>, whom she met while filming <i><a href="/wiki/Planet_of_the_Apes_(2001_film)" title="Planet of the Apes (2001 film)">Planet of the Apes</a></i>. Burton subsequently took to casting her in his films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Fish_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Fish (film)">Big Fish</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Corpse_Bride" title="Corpse Bride">Corpse Bride</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory_(film)" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (film)">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sweeney_Todd:_The_Demon_Barber_of_Fleet_Street_(2007_film)" title="Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street (2007 film)">Sweeney Todd: The Demon Barber of Fleet Street</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Shadows_(film)" title="Dark Shadows (film)">Dark Shadows</a></i>. After their separation, Bonham Carter mentioned, "it might be easier to work together without being together any more. He always only cast me with great embarrassment."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonham Carter and Burton lived in adjoining houses in <a href="/wiki/Belsize_Park" title="Belsize Park">Belsize Park</a>, London. Bonham Carter owned one of the houses; Burton later purchased the other and they connected the two. In 2006, they bought the <a href="/wiki/Mill_House_and_The_Wharf,_Sutton_Courtenay" title="Mill House and The Wharf, Sutton Courtenay">Mill House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sutton_Courtenay" title="Sutton Courtenay">Sutton Courtenay</a>. It was previously leased by her grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Violet_Bonham_Carter" title="Violet Bonham Carter">Violet Bonham Carter</a>, and owned by her great-grandfather <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonham Carter and Burton have two children together: son Billy Raymond Burton<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and daughter Nell Burton.<sup id="cite_ref-nell_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nell-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter has stated that her daughter Nell is named after all the "Helens" in her family.<sup id="cite_ref-JJ_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JJ-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nell_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nell-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Bonham Carter told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> of her struggles with <a href="/wiki/Infertility" title="Infertility">infertility</a> and the difficulties she had during her pregnancies. She noted that before the conception of her daughter, she and Burton had been trying for a baby for two years and although they conceived naturally, they were considering <a href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation" title="In vitro fertilisation">in vitro fertilisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 December 2014, Bonham Carter and Burton announced that they had "separated amicably" earlier that year.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Of the separation, Bonham Carter told <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Bazaar" title="Harper&#39;s Bazaar">Harper's Bazaar</a></i>: "Everyone always says you have to be strong and have a stiff upper lip, but it's okay to be fragile.... You've got to take very small steps, and sometimes you won't know where to go next because you've lost yourself." She added: "With divorce, you go through massive grief—it is a death of a relationship, so it's utterly bewildering. Your identity, everything, changes."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bonham Carter is known for her unconventional and eccentric sense of fashion.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> named her on its 2010 Best-Dressed List<sup id="cite_ref-vanity_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanity-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and she was selected by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a> to be the face of his autumn/winter 2011 advertising campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> She has cited <a href="/wiki/Vivienne_Westwood" title="Vivienne Westwood">Vivienne Westwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">Marie Antoinette</a> as her main style influences.<sup id="cite_ref-vanity_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanity-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paternal">Paternal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Paternal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bonham_Carter_family" title="Bonham Carter family">Bonham Carter family</a></div>
<p>Bonham Carter's paternal grandparents were British <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal politicians</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bonham-Carter" title="Maurice Bonham-Carter">Maurice Bonham-Carter</a> and Lady <a href="/wiki/Violet_Bonham_Carter" title="Violet Bonham Carter">Violet Bonham Carter</a>. Helena is descended on her father's side from <a href="/wiki/John_Bonham-Carter_(1788%E2%80%931838)" title="John Bonham-Carter (1788–1838)">John Bonham Carter</a>, Member of Parliament for Portsmouth. Helena's paternal great-grandfather was <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H.&#160;H. Asquith</a>, 1st Earl of Oxford and Asquith and Prime Minister of Britain 1908–1916. She is the great-niece of Asquith's son, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Asquith" title="Anthony Asquith">Anthony Asquith</a>, English director of such films as <i><a href="/wiki/Carrington_V.C._(film)" title="Carrington V.C. (film)">Carrington V.C.</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Importance_of_Being_Earnest_(1952_film)" title="The Importance of Being Earnest (1952 film)">The Importance of Being Earnest</a></i>, and a first cousin of the economist <a href="/wiki/Adam_Ridley" title="Adam Ridley">Adam Ridley</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and of politician <a href="/wiki/Jane_Bonham_Carter,_Baroness_Bonham-Carter_of_Yarnbury" title="Jane Bonham Carter, Baroness Bonham-Carter of Yarnbury">Jane Bonham Carter</a>.
</p><p>Bonham Carter is a distant cousin of actor <a href="/wiki/Crispin_Bonham-Carter" title="Crispin Bonham-Carter">Crispin Bonham-Carter</a>. Other prominent distant relatives include <a href="/wiki/Lothian_Bonham-Carter" title="Lothian Bonham-Carter">Lothian Bonham Carter</a>, who played <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> for <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Hampshire County Cricket Club">Hampshire</a>, his son, Vice Admiral Sir <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Bonham_Carter" title="Stuart Bonham Carter">Stuart Bonham Carter</a>, who served in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> in both <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">world wars</a>, and pioneering English nurse <a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maternal">Maternal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Maternal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fould_family" title="Fould family">Fould family</a></div>
<p>Her maternal grandfather, Spanish diplomat <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Propper_de_Callej%C3%B3n" title="Eduardo Propper de Callejón">Eduardo Propper de Callejón</a>, saved thousands of Jews from the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, for which he was recognised as <a href="/wiki/Righteous_Among_the_Nations" title="Righteous Among the Nations">Righteous Among the Nations</a> (his own father was a Bohemian Jew).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He later served as Minister-Counselor at the Spanish Embassy in Washington, D.C.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her maternal grandmother, Baroness Hélène Fould-Springer, was from an upper class <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> family; she was the daughter of Baron Eugène Fould-Springer (a French banker descended from the <a href="/wiki/Ephrussi_family" title="Ephrussi family">Ephrussi family</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fould_family" title="Fould family">Fould dynasty</a>) and Marie Cecile von Springer (whose father was Austrian-born industrialist Baron Gustav von Springer, and whose mother was from the de <a href="/wiki/Koenigswarter" title="Koenigswarter">Koenigswarter</a> family).<sup id="cite_ref-Costa2006-11-03_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costa2006-11-03-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-08ref1_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08ref1-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Hélène Fould-Springer converted to Catholicism after the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Hélène's sister was the French philanthropist Liliane de Rothschild (1916–2003), the wife of Baron <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lie_de_Rothschild" title="Élie de Rothschild">Élie de Rothschild</a>, of the prominent <a href="/wiki/Rothschild_family" title="Rothschild family">Rothschild family</a> (who had also married within the von Springer family in the 19th century);<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Liliane's other sister, Therese Fould-Springer, was the mother of British writer <a href="/wiki/David_Pryce-Jones" title="David Pryce-Jones">David Pryce-Jones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-08ref1_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08ref1-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Helena_Bonham_Carter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="List of awards and nominations received by Helena Bonham Carter">List of awards and nominations received by Helena Bonham Carter</a></div>
<p>Bonham Carter has been the recipient of a <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA Award">BAFTA Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Critics&#39; Choice Movie Award">Critics' Choice Movie Award</a>, an <a href="/wiki/International_Emmy_Award" title="International Emmy Award">International Emmy Award</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award" title="Screen Actors Guild Award">Screen Actors Guild Award</a>, as well as receiving further nominations for two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>, seven <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Awards</a> and three <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award" title="Primetime Emmy Award">Primetime Emmy Awards</a>. She has received other prestigious awards such as a <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Film_Critics_Association_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Film Critics Association Award">Los Angeles Film Critics Association Award</a> and two <a href="/wiki/National_Board_of_Review" title="National Board of Review">National Board of Review</a> awards.<sup id="cite_ref-KingsSpeech_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KingsSpeech-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
